Local Boston chefs like <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/kenoringer\">Kenny Oringer<\/a> of Toro and Clio, <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/SteveDiFillippo\">Steve DiFillippo<\/a> from Davio&#8217;s, Jay Hajj from <a href=\"http:\/\/www.mikescitydiner.com\/\">Mike&#8217;s City Diner<\/a>, Paul Malvone of the <a href=\"http:\/\/www.bostonburgerco.com\/\">Boston Burger Co.<\/a>, and Tony DiCenso of <a href=\"http:\/\/www.rinosplace.com\/\">Rino&#8217;s Place<\/a>, partnered up with Buddies to cook a killer meal for everyone at the kickoff event after they worked up a healthy appetite at Harvard Stadium. Each Buddy had met with their chef mentor earlier that month for several on-site visits to learn the ins and outs of a restaurant kitchen as well as practice making their signature dish for the event. He credits much of his success in business and cooking to the knowledge he gained while operating his cart, and he wants to pay it forward! Through his Cooking With Kids Foundation, he&#8217;s offering The Awesome Pretzel Cart.<\/p>\n<p>Nonprofit clubs or groups that serve young people throughout the country can raise money to purchase a cart, and CWK will fund half of the cost to qualified organizations. The cart can be used to sell healthy and delicious whole wheat pretzels at events in the community. All proceeds from pretzel sales will go back into the youth-based organization that owns the cart. This is an opportunity for young people to learn money management, marketing, food preparation, teamwork, and more!<\/p>\n<p>To learn more about the program, visit the <a href=\"http:\/\/www.cwkfoundation.org\/pretzelcart\/\">Awesome Pretzel Cart<\/a> section on the Cooking With Kids Foundation website. It\u2019s really the first big father\u2019s day thing we\u2019ve planned with Hunter since he was born. We pack a picnic, with sandwiches in Ziploc bags, got a cooler filled up to the top, the whole nine yards. We go to the rental shop to get the canoes, they\u2019re giving us instructions ask if we\u2019ve done this before, me and my dad are like of course. They give very specific instructions for this one part of the river, and they tell us to stay to the left, because if you go to hard to the right, you\u2019ll get sucked into the brush and most likely flip the canoe.<\/p>\n<p>We\u2019re going down the river, we see the turn, me and my dad are rowing &#8211; we don\u2019t communicate, the canoe flips over, I get tossed out, the cooler gets dumped, my dad\u2019s underneath the canoe, I look up and Hunter is floating down the river. Hunter\u2019s about a hundred yards down -stream standing their picking our soaked food out of the river and gathering our Ziploc bagged sandwiches.<\/p>\n<p>I end up having to drag the canoe the rest of the way down the river by a rope line from the bank. It was just one of those father\u2019s days that we look back on and laugh about.
